# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Grafana Dashboard JSON Model Version Migration

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in grafana/grafana that implement dashboard JSON model versioning and migration: the dashboard version schema definitions, the DashboardMigrator, and the field-level migration functions that upgrade old dashboard JSON to the current schema version.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

The migration system supports dashboard schema versions 0-42, with version 42 being the final version for the v1 dashboard API.\\n\\n## Core Migration Infrastructure (apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/)\\n\\nThe main migration orchestrator is in **migrate.go**, which implements the `Migrate()` function that manages the complete migration pipeline. It performs sequential steps: cleanup of backend-only properties, application of frontend defaults, panel defaults assignment, unique ID generation, and then executes individual schema version migrations.\\n\\nThe **migrations.go** file in the schemaversion package defines the `SchemaVersionMigrationFunc` type and the `GetMigrations()` registry that returns a map of all version migrations (v2-v42). It also provides utility functions like `GetSchemaVersion()` to extract and normalize schema versions from dashboard JSON.\\n\\n## Field-Level Migration Functions (apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/)\\n\\nIndividual schema version migrations are implemented as separate files (v2.go through v42.go, totaling 41 migration functions). This includes default values for title, timezone, time range, panels, targets, and grid positions. The `applyPanelDefaults()` function ensures every panel has baseline properties like gridPos and targets.\\n\\n## API Version Conversion\\n\\nThe conversion subsystem in **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/** handles cross-version API conversions between v0alpha1, v1beta1, v2alpha1, and v2beta1 dashboard types. **conversion.go** registers conversion functions between all API version pairs, while individual conversion files (v0.go, v1.go, v2.go, v2alpha1_to_v2beta1.go) implement the actual conversion logic using Kubernetes conversion scopes.\\n\\n## Schema Definitions\\n\\nDashboard API schema definitions are versioned in **apps/dashboard/pkg/apis/dashboard/**:\\n- **v0alpha1, v1beta1, v2alpha1, v2beta1**: Each contains types.go, constants.go, dashboard_spec.go for their respective API versions\\n- **types.go & utils.go** in the parent directory provide shared types and utilities\\n- **apps/dashboard/pkg/apis/dashboard/v0alpha1/dashboard_spec.go** and similar files contain the actual spec definitions\\n\\nThe **HandoffSchemaVersion** constant (value 36) defined in **pkg/kinds/dashboard/addenda.go** marks the minimum schema version at which the Thema-based schema becomes valid. Dashboards below this version require the TypeScript migration logic to run first.\\n\\n## Error Handling and Metrics\\n\\n**errors.go** defines MigrationError and MinimumVersionError types for comprehensive error reporting. **metrics.go** tracks migration success and failure metrics with counters for dashboard migrations.\\n\\n## Test Infrastructure\\n\\nEach schema version migration has corresponding test files (v2_test.go through v42_test.go). versioning and migration through a multi-layered architecture spanning backend Go code and frontend TypeScript. The migration system supports dashboard schema versions 0-42, with version 42 being the final version for the v1 dashboard API.\\n\\n## Core Migration Infrastructure (apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/)\\n\\nThe main migration orchestrator is in **migrate.go**, which implements the `Migrate()` function that manages the complete migration pipeline. It performs sequential steps: cleanup of backend-only properties, application of frontend defaults, panel defaults assignment, unique ID generation, and then executes individual schema version migrations.\\n\\nThe **migrations.go** file in the schemaversion package defines the `SchemaVersionMigrationFunc` type and the `GetMigrations()` registry that returns a map of all version migrations (v2-v42). It also provides utility functions like `GetSchemaVersion()` to extract and normalize schema versions from dashboard JSON.\\n\\n## Field-Level Migration Functions (apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/)\\n\\nIndividual schema version migrations are implemented as separate files (v2.go through v42.go, totaling 41 migration functions). Key migrations include:\\n\\n- **V2**: Handles legacy services.filter structure migrations\\n- **V6**: Moves dropdown annotations to new schema\\n- **V7**: Converts nav property to timepicker\\n- **V9**: Removes first threshold value from singlestat panel thresholds\\n- **V14**: Migrates sharedCrosshair boolean to graphTooltip integer\\n- **V16**: Implements the row-based to grid-based layout migration (the largest migration)\\n- **V28**: Performs variable and panel transformation updates\\n- **V33**: Handles DataSource reference migrations with DataSourceInfoProvider\\n- **V36**: Updates panel options and field configurations\\n- **V38**: Migrates table display modes to cell options\\n- **V41 & V42**: Final schema version updates\\n\\nUtility functions in **migration_utils.go** provide type-safe value extraction from maps, including `GetStringValue()`, `GetBoolValue()`, `GetIntValue()`, and `GetFloatValue()`, ensuring consistent handling of type conversions throughout migrations.\\n\\n## Frontend Defaults Application\\n\\nThe **frontend_defaults.go** file applies all DashboardModel and PanelModel constructor defaults before migrations run, matching the frontend's behavior. This includes default values for title, timezone, time range, panels, targets, and grid positions. The `applyPanelDefaults()` function ensures every panel has baseline properties like gridPos and targets.\\n\\n## API Version Conversion\\n\\nThe conversion subsystem in **apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/** handles cross-version API conversions between v0alpha1, v1beta1, v2alpha1, and v2beta1 dashboard types. **conversion.go** registers conversion functions between all API version pairs, while individual conversion files (v0.go, v1.go, v2.go, v2alpha1_to_v2beta1.go) implement the actual conversion logic using Kubernetes conversion scopes.\\n\\n## Schema Definitions\\n\\nDashboard API schema definitions are versioned in **apps/dashboard/pkg/apis/dashboard/**:\\n- **v0alpha1, v1beta1, v2alpha1, v2beta1**: Each contains types.go, constants.go, dashboard_spec.go for their respective API versions\\n- **types.go & utils.go** in the parent directory provide shared types and utilities\\n- **apps/dashboard/pkg/apis/dashboard/v0alpha1/dashboard_spec.go** and similar files contain the actual spec definitions\\n\\nThe **HandoffSchemaVersion** constant (value 36) defined in **pkg/kinds/dashboard/addenda.go** marks the minimum schema version at which the Thema-based schema becomes valid. Dashboards below this version require the TypeScript migration logic to run first.\\n\\n## Error Handling and Metrics\\n\\n**errors.go** defines MigrationError and MinimumVersionError types for comprehensive error reporting. **metrics.go** tracks migration success and failure metrics with counters for dashboard migrations.\\n\\n## Test Infrastructure\\n\\nEach schema version migration has corresponding test files (v2_test.go through v42_test.go).
